     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with a ruptured large right middle cerebral
     artery bifurcation aneurysm and an anterior communicating artery aneurysm with
     a daughter segment.  Status post coil embolization of the right middle
     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450

                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

     * -59 DISTINCT PROCEDURAL SERVICE      36218 ADD'L 2ND/3RD ORDER           *
     * 75894 TRANSCATH EMBO THERAPY         75894 TRANSCATH EMBO THERAPY        *
     * -59 DISTINCT PROCEDURAL SERVICE      75898 F/U TRANS CATH THERAPY        *
     * 75898 F/U TRANS CATH THERAPY         75680 CAROTID/CEREBRAL BILAT        *
     * 75671 CAROTID/CEREBRAL BILAT         75685 VERT/CAROTID A-GRAM           *
     * 75685 VERT/CAROTID A-GRAM            -59 DISTINCT PROCEDURAL SERVICE     *
     * 75716 EXT BILAT A-GRAM               -52 REDUCED SERVICES                *
     * 75774 SEL EA ADD'L                                                       *
     ****************************************************************************
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with a ruptured large right middle cerebral
     artery bifurcation aneurysm and an anterior communicating artery aneurysm with
     a daughter segment.  Status post coil embolization of the right middle
     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

                                     FINAL REPORT
     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with a ruptured large right middle cerebral
     artery bifurcation aneurysm and an anterior communicating artery aneurysm with
     a daughter segment.  Status post coil embolization of the right middle
     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter

     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.

     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

                                     FINAL REPORT
     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with a ruptured large right middle cerebral
     artery bifurcation aneurysm and an anterior communicating artery aneurysm with
     a daughter segment.  Status post coil embolization of the right middle
     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with a ruptured large right middle cerebral
     artery bifurcation aneurysm and an anterior communicating artery aneurysm with
     a daughter segment.  Status post coil embolization of the right middle
     cerebral artery via a right internal carotid artery microcatheter approach and
     status post coil embolization of the anterior communicating artery through a
     left internal carotid artery microcatheter based approach.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     A series of angiographic runs were performed including biplane runs which
     revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and near complete obliteration of the
     aneurysm with its coils.  At this point, biplane angiographic runs were
     performed of the left internal carotid artery to document the final result and
     the patient was transferred back to intensive care in stable condition.  There
     was no elevation of the intracranial pressure and the patient was administered
     a dose of intravenous heparin which was graded beginning with a very low dose
     and after deployment of a few coils into the right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm was taken to an ACT closer to then greater than 200 seconds.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm and anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm treated via a right internal carotid artery and
     left internal carotid artery approaches respectively using microcatheter-based
     GDC coils.

     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a 63 year old woman who had a high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage characterized by a right sylvian fissure clot.  After
     a period of a poorly reacting right pupil at the outside hospital, her pupils
     had since become equal and reactive and she is undergoing the cerebral
     angiogram in order to diagnose the source of the hemorrhage and also to
     provide endovascular treatment.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient's husband and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient's husband and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-6-23**] 6:06 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2131**]
     Reason: ? ANUERYSM
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 450
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right subclavian
     artery, right vertebral artery, left common carotid artery, left internal
     carotid artery, left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.  At this
     point, evaluation of the patient's vessels revealed no evidence of carotid
     disease in the cervical bifurcation or intracranially.  Injection of the right
     internal carotid artery revealed the presence of a large anteriorly pointing
     middle cerebral artery bifurcation aneurysm measuring approximately 12 to 15
     mm in greatest diameter by 9 mm with a 6 to 7 mm neck.  There is a daughter
     aneurysm near the region of the neck which is probably of the rupture site. In
     addition, injection of the left internal carotid artery reveals the presence
     of a dominant left A1 segment in the anterior cerebral artery and an
     approximately 6 mm aneurysm with a daughter component which represents a high
     risk for subsequent rupture.  Injection of the bilateral subclavian arteries
     were within normal limits as were the vertebral arteries with no evidence of
     stenosis in the cervical segment or intracranially.  There is no evidence of
     posterior circulation aneurysm.  At this point, a decision was made to proceed
     with endovascular coil embolization using a two-stage approach.  The initial
     procedure centered treatment of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm to
     that end.  The patient underwent placement of a 5 FR guide catheter into the
     right internal carotid artery.  Through that catheter a XL 10 microcatheter
     was guided over a microwire into the supraclinoid internal carotid artery
     across the intracranial bifurcation into the right middle cerebral artery and
     finally into the aneurysm.  With the microcatheter in this position and after
     obtaining a series of three-dimensional angiographic runs to obtain the best
     projection, a series of GDC coils were deployed into the aneurysm under
     constant surveillance.  These began with a GDC 10 3D 10 mm x 30 cm and
     continued for a total of 18 coils ending a GDC ultrasoft 2 [**12-18**] x 3 cm.  The
     last coil was not deployed because of herniation one of the middle cerebral
     artery branches and accordingly was removed.  Multiple surveillance mid
     embolization and post embolization three dimensional and biplane angiographic
     runs are performed which revealed no evidence of branch occlusion and showed
     good embolization of the aneurysm including the daughter aneurysm near the
     neck which was felt to be the rupture site.  At this point, the microcatheter
     was removed from the middle cerebral artery aneurysm and our attention was
     turned towards treatment of the left internal carotid artery approach leading
     to the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  To that end, an SL 10
     microcatheter streamed shaped and the microwire was given a S-shaped and the
     microcatheter was navigated through the left internal carotid artery after
     placement of the guide catheter into the left internal carotid artery.  The
     microcatheter was guided into the left A1 segment of the anterior cerebral
     artery and then into the anterior communicating artery aneurysm.  With the
     microcath in this position, a series of GDC coils were deployed for a total of
     7 coils beginning with a GDC 3D 4 x 6 and ending a GDC 2 mm x 1 cm ultrasoft.

     structures towards the left, not significantly changed in extent.  There is
     mild-moderate effacement of the basilar cisterns.  The visualized osseous

     uncal/hippocampal herniation. There has been no significant change from the
     prior outside CT done several hours earlier.

     likely representing atherosclerotic calcification in a right middle cerebral
     artery aneursym, presumably the source of the subarachnoid hemorrhage.

     brachiocephalic vein.  This again demonstrated some near occlusion of the left
     brachiocephalic vein, with patency of the superior vena cava.

     brachiocephalic vein.  This again demonstrated some near occlusion of the left
     brachiocephalic vein, with patency of the superior vena cava.
     
     The right subclavian catheter was then pulled back approximately 5-6 cm, so
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2832-7-18**] 4:16 PM
     IVC GRAM/FILTER                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2160**]
     Reason: please place a SVC filter in a patient with an UE DVT       
     Admitting Diagnosis: SUBARACHNOID HEMORRHAGE
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 70
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     that the tip was in the superior vena cava.  Over a guide wire, a 6-French
     sheath was advanced to the level of the superior vena cava, and an Optease
     inferior vena caval filter was then deployed under fluoroscopic guidance in
     the superior vena cava.  The medial aspect of the filter was noted to be
     somewhat indented after placement, most likely due to arterial pulsations. The
     hook of the filter is caudal, so that if retrieval is an option, a femoral
     approach is essential.
     
     The sheath was then removed, compression was applied over the right groin
     until hemostasis achieved.
     
     COMPLICATIONS:  None.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Successful placement of an Optease retrievable superior vena
     caval filter from a right femoral venous approach.  The filter can be removed
     up to two weeks post placement.

     weeks previously.  The patient presents with left upper extremity swelling,
     and an ultrasound revealed thrombus in the left subclavian, axillary and
     brachial veins.  Please place superior vena caval filter.
     
     REFERRING PHYSICIAN:  [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 527**]. [**First Name8 (NamePattern2) **] [**Name (STitle) 726**].
     
     INTERVENTIONAL RADIOLOGIST:  Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) 346**].  Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) 2161**], Radiology Resident,
     assisted in the procedure.
     
     CONTRAST/MEDICATIONS:  70 cc Optiray 320 at 60%.
     
     PROCEDURE/FINDINGS:  The procedure was described to the patient's next of [**Doctor First Name **],
     and informed consent was obtained.  Access was gained into the right femoral
     vein using a 19-gauge single-wall needle.  [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 528**] wire was advanced without
     difficulty into the superior vena cava, followed by placement of a 4-French
     sheath.  A 4-French multi-side-hole straight catheter was then used to select
     the right internal jugular vein, and a superior venacavagram was performed
     with the catheter in the right internal jugular vein.  This demonstrated some
     thrombus in and around the right subclavian catheter, whose distal tip is in
     the mid superior vena cava.  There was some reflux of contrast into the distal
     left brachiocephalic vein.
     
     We then selected the left brachiocephalic vein using a 0.035 angled Glidewire,
     and gently manipulated the wire and catheter to the mid portion of the
     presumed left brachiocephalic vein.  However, on aspiration, no blood was
     demonstrated.  A small contrast injection was then performed, documenting near
     occlusion of the left brachiocephalic vein, with a tiny collateral branch
     patent.  The catheter was then pulled into the distal left brachiocephalic
     vein, until blood could be aspirated from the catheter.  We performed a
     superior venacavagram at this time with the catheter in the distal left
     brachiocephalic vein.  This again demonstrated some near occlusion of the left
     brachiocephalic vein, with patency of the superior vena cava.
     
     The right subclavian catheter was then pulled back approximately 5-6 cm, so

     that the tip was in the superior vena cava.  Over a guide wire, a 6-French
     sheath was advanced to the level of the superior vena cava, and an Optease
     inferior vena caval filter was then deployed under fluoroscopic guidance in
     the superior vena cava.  The medial aspect of the filter was noted to be
     somewhat indented after placement, most likely due to arterial pulsations. The
     hook of the filter is caudal, so that if retrieval is an option, a femoral
     approach is essential.
     
     The sheath was then removed, compression was applied over the right groin
     until hemostasis achieved.
     
     COMPLICATIONS:  None.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Successful placement of an Optease retrievable superior vena
     caval filter from a right femoral venous approach.  The filter can be removed
     up to two weeks post placement.

     DATE: [**2833-2-9**] 7:37 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2176**]
     Reason: 2:00PM
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 218
     ********************************* CPT Codes ********************************
     * 36217 SEL CATH 3RD ORDER [**Last Name (un) 7**]        36216 SEL CATH 2ND ORDER            *
     * -59 DISTINCT PROCEDURAL SERVICE      36216 SEL CATH 2ND ORDER            *
     * -59 DISTINCT PROCEDURAL SERVICE      36218 ADD'L 2ND/3RD ORDER           *
     * 75680 CAROTID/CEREBRAL BILAT         75671 CAROTID/CEREBRAL BILAT        *
     * 75660 EXT CAROTID UNILAT             75685 VERT/CAROTID A-GRAM           *
     * 75710 EXT UNILAT A-GRAM              -52 REDUCED SERVICES                *
     * C1760 CLOSURE DEVICE VASC IMP/INS    C1894 INT/SHTH NOT/GUID EP NON-LASER*
     ****************************************************************************
     ______________________________________________________________________________
     UNDERLYING MEDICAL CONDITION:
      63 year old woman with aneurysm.
     REASON FOR THIS EXAMINATION:
      SAME DAY ADMIT.  START TIME 9:30.  Cerebral angiogram with possible coiling of
      aneurysm.
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Previously ruptured right middle cerebral artery
     aneurysm and unruptured anterior communicating artery aneurysm and high grade
     subarachnoid hemorrhage.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same with interval aneurysmal regrowth of the right
     middle cerebral artery aneurysm at the neck and stable appearance of the
     previously treated anterior communicating artery aneurysm.
     
     INDICATION:  Mr. [**Known patient firstname 2177**] [**Known patient lastname 2132**] suffered a high grade subarachnoid hemorrhage
     from the ruptured right middle cerebral artery aneurysm.  She underwent
     endovascular therapy of this aneurysm as well as an unruptured anterior
     communicating artery aneurysm from the left-sided approach and subsequently
     underwent emergent craniectomy for elevated intracranial pressure.  Following
     a protracted hospital course, she has since had a significant improvement in
     her neurological status in rehabilitation and is currently undergoing cerebral
     angiogram to follow up on the previously treated aneurysm.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient, her husband, and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient, her husband, and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 4 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-2-9**] 7:37 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2176**]
     Reason: 2:00PM
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 218
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, left common
     carotid artery, left internal carotid artery, left external carotid artery,
     left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.
     
     RESULTS:  Injection of the right common carotid artery showed the presence of
     a 30% atherosclerotic stenosis in the cervical region of the right internal
     carotid artery origin.  Injection of the right internal carotid artery with
     three dimensional rotational angiography showed the presence of a new regrowth
     at the aneurysm neck measuring approximately 8 mm x 4 mm.  This will be
     treated in the future but may require the use of an endovascular stent.
     Accordingly the patient will be placed on antibiotic therapy prior to the next
     treatment session.  Injection of the left common carotid artery shows 20%
     atherosclerotic disease at the origin of the left internal carotid artery into
     the neck.  Injection of the left internal carotid artery intracranially showed
     filling of the anterior communicating artery with stable appearance of the
     previously treated ACOM aneurysm.  The proximal portion of the right A2
     segment which fills the left ICA injection shows a small aneurysmal dilatation
     of approximately 1 1/2 mm in depth which is unchanged compared to a previous
     procedure.  Injection of the left external carotid artery was within normal
     limits.  Injection of the left subclavian artery showed a 30% atherosclerotic
     shelf proximal to the origin of left vertebral artery.  Injection of the left
     vertebral artery showed no atherosclerotic involvement of the left vertebral
     artery at its origin.  The cervical course of the left vertebral artery was
     normal and intracranially the left vertebral artery was dominant with a normal
     appearance of the basilar artery and its branches.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Interval regrowth of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm
     and its neck which will be retreated and stable appearance of the previously
     treated anterior communicating artery aneurysm.

     CONSENT:  The patient, her husband, and her son were given a full and complete
     explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks, benefits
     and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In addition the
     possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection, stroke,
     neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other unforeseen
     complications including the risk of coma and even death were outlined.  The
     patient, her husband, and her son understood and wished to proceed with the
     operation.
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge single wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 4 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire and kept
     on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-2-9**] 7:37 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2176**]
     Reason: 2:00PM
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 218
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, left common
     carotid artery, left internal carotid artery, left external carotid artery,
     left subclavian artery, and left vertebral artery.
     
     RESULTS:  Injection of the right common carotid artery showed the presence of
     a 30% atherosclerotic stenosis in the cervical region of the right internal
     carotid artery origin.  Injection of the right internal carotid artery with
     three dimensional rotational angiography showed the presence of a new regrowth
     at the aneurysm neck measuring approximately 8 mm x 4 mm.  This will be
     treated in the future but may require the use of an endovascular stent.
     Accordingly the patient will be placed on antibiotic therapy prior to the next
     treatment session.  Injection of the left common carotid artery shows 20%
     atherosclerotic disease at the origin of the left internal carotid artery into
     the neck.  Injection of the left internal carotid artery intracranially showed
     filling of the anterior communicating artery with stable appearance of the
     previously treated ACOM aneurysm.  The proximal portion of the right A2
     segment which fills the left ICA injection shows a small aneurysmal dilatation
     of approximately 1 1/2 mm in depth which is unchanged compared to a previous
     procedure.  Injection of the left external carotid artery was within normal
     limits.  Injection of the left subclavian artery showed a 30% atherosclerotic
     shelf proximal to the origin of left vertebral artery.  Injection of the left
     vertebral artery showed no atherosclerotic involvement of the left vertebral
     artery at its origin.  The cervical course of the left vertebral artery was
     normal and intracranially the left vertebral artery was dominant with a normal
     appearance of the basilar artery and its branches.
     
     IMPRESSION:  Interval regrowth of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm
     and its neck which will be retreated and stable appearance of the previously
     treated anterior communicating artery aneurysm.

     procedure.  Injection of the left external carotid artery was within normal
     limits.  Injection of the left subclavian artery showed a 30% atherosclerotic
     shelf proximal to the origin of left vertebral artery.  Injection of the left
     vertebral artery showed no atherosclerotic involvement of the left vertebral
     artery at its origin.  The cervical course of the left vertebral artery was
     normal and intracranially the left vertebral artery was dominant with a normal
     appearance of the basilar artery and its branches.

     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a patient who suffered a high grade subarachnoid
     hemorrhage requiring craniectomy and a prolonged stay in the intensive care
     unit followed by extensive rehabilitation.  She has made an excellent recovery
     which has left her with mild left-sided hemiparesis.  At the time of her
     initial treatment, the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm which was noted
     to be wide neck could not be treated completely at the neck although the
     rupture site was secured with coils and the patient did an excellent recovery.
     The neck of the aneurysm was relatively loosely packed because its wide neck.
     Accordingly she is undergoing this procedure in order to perform a stent
     mediated coil embolization and packing of the neck of the right middle
     cerebral aneurysm.

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge signal wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire
     and kept on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right middle
     cerebral artery, right M3 branch of the middle cerebral artery.  After the
     patient has been placed on Plavix and desensitize using gradual dosage of
     aspirin, a procedure was scheduled and the patient was brought to the
     endovascular suite.  The guide catheter was then used to selectively
     catheterize the right common carotid artery with an angiographic run revealed
     the presence of diffuse atherosclerotic disease which is unchanged compared to
     previously.  Angiographic run was performed then of the right internal carotid
     and biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography mode which helpded
     define the wide neck of the aneurysm and the pocket of loosely packed coils.
     At this point, a  microcatheter was used coaxially over a 200 cm exchange MPI
     wire.  The MTI X-celerator wire was then used to selectively place the
     microcatheter into the inferior division of the middle cerebral artery on the
     right side. With the microcatheter in this branch, the wire was advanced well
     into M3 branch consistent with the angular branch of the angular division of
     the middle cerebral artery.  The microcatheter was then removed and a
     neuroform stent was guided over the exchange wire and delivered across the
     cerebral artery bifurcation.  This unable us then to keep the stent in
     position.  After deployment an angiographic run was performed which showed no
     evidence of branch occlusion or compromise by the stent deployed.
     Subsequently, the wire was withdrawn up to the middle cerebral artery location
     and the microcatheter  was then used to cross the interstices of the stent
     into the neck residual.  With the microcatheter in the aneurysm, residual
     series of GDC coils were advanced until they were clearly in contact with the
     stent interstices.  At this point, an angiographic run was performed in
     biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography which showed an excellent
     result.  The microcatheter was then withdrawn and a final angiographic run was
     performed in the biplane projection as well as one of the neck which showed no
     evidence of intimal injury to the carotid artery.  At this point, the guide
     catheter was withdrawn.  The patient was then awokened from anesthesia and
     transferred to the post anesthesia care unit in stable condition.
     
     RESULTS:  Persistent 4 mm pocket of the previously treated right middle
     cerebral aneurysm embolized using a combination of GDC coils and neuroform
     stent with an excellent angiographic result with no evidence of iatrogenic
     branch occlusion.
