     PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Grade 5 previously ruptured aneurysm status post
     endovascular coil embolization with neurological recovery now showing evidence
     of persistent loosely packed coils at the origin of the right middle cerebral
     artery.
     
     POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS:  Same.  Status post stent mediated coil embolization
     of the neck of the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm.
     
     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a patient who suffered a high grade subarachnoid
     hemorrhage requiring craniectomy and a prolonged stay in the intensive care
     unit followed by extensive rehabilitation.  She has made an excellent recovery
     which has left her with mild left-sided hemiparesis.  At the time of her
     initial treatment, the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm which was noted
     to be wide neck could not be treated completely at the neck although the
     rupture site was secured with coils and the patient did an excellent recovery.
     The neck of the aneurysm was relatively loosely packed because its wide neck.
     Accordingly she is undergoing this procedure in order to perform a stent
     mediated coil embolization and packing of the neck of the right middle
     cerebral aneurysm.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient and her son and her husband were given a full and
     complete explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks,
     benefits and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In
     addition the possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection,
     stroke, neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other
     unforeseen complications including the risk of coma and even death were
     outlined.  The patient and her son and her husband understood and wished to
     proceed with the operation.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge signal wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire
     and kept on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right middle
     cerebral artery, right M3 branch of the middle cerebral artery.  After the
     patient has been placed on Plavix and desensitize using gradual dosage of
     aspirin, a procedure was scheduled and the patient was brought to the
     endovascular suite.  The guide catheter was then used to selectively
     catheterize the right common carotid artery with an angiographic run revealed
     the presence of diffuse atherosclerotic disease which is unchanged compared to
     previously.  Angiographic run was performed then of the right internal carotid
     and biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography mode which helpded
     define the wide neck of the aneurysm and the pocket of loosely packed coils.
     At this point, a  microcatheter was used coaxially over a 200 cm exchange MPI
     wire.  The MTI X-celerator wire was then used to selectively place the
     microcatheter into the inferior division of the middle cerebral artery on the
     right side. With the microcatheter in this branch, the wire was advanced well
     into M3 branch consistent with the angular branch of the angular division of
     the middle cerebral artery.  The microcatheter was then removed and a
     neuroform stent was guided over the exchange wire and delivered across the
     cerebral artery bifurcation.  This unable us then to keep the stent in
     position.  After deployment an angiographic run was performed which showed no
     evidence of branch occlusion or compromise by the stent deployed.
     Subsequently, the wire was withdrawn up to the middle cerebral artery location
     and the microcatheter  was then used to cross the interstices of the stent
     into the neck residual.  With the microcatheter in the aneurysm, residual
     series of GDC coils were advanced until they were clearly in contact with the
     stent interstices.  At this point, an angiographic run was performed in
     biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography which showed an excellent
     result.  The microcatheter was then withdrawn and a final angiographic run was
     performed in the biplane projection as well as one of the neck which showed no
     evidence of intimal injury to the carotid artery.  At this point, the guide
     catheter was withdrawn.  The patient was then awokened from anesthesia and
     transferred to the post anesthesia care unit in stable condition.
     
     RESULTS:  Persistent 4 mm pocket of the previously treated right middle
     cerebral aneurysm embolized using a combination of GDC coils and neuroform
     stent with an excellent angiographic result with no evidence of iatrogenic
     branch occlusion.
     
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268

     ANESTHESIA:  General endotracheal anesthesia.
     
     INDICATION:  Ms. [**Known patient lastname 2132**] is a patient who suffered a high grade subarachnoid
     hemorrhage requiring craniectomy and a prolonged stay in the intensive care
     unit followed by extensive rehabilitation.  She has made an excellent recovery
     which has left her with mild left-sided hemiparesis.  At the time of her
     initial treatment, the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm which was noted
     to be wide neck could not be treated completely at the neck although the
     rupture site was secured with coils and the patient did an excellent recovery.
     The neck of the aneurysm was relatively loosely packed because its wide neck.
     Accordingly she is undergoing this procedure in order to perform a stent
     mediated coil embolization and packing of the neck of the right middle
     cerebral aneurysm.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient and her son and her husband were given a full and
     complete explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks,
     benefits and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In
     addition the possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection,
     stroke, neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other
     unforeseen complications including the risk of coma and even death were
     outlined.  The patient and her son and her husband understood and wished to
     proceed with the operation.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge signal wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire
     and kept on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right middle
     cerebral artery, right M3 branch of the middle cerebral artery.  After the
     patient has been placed on Plavix and desensitize using gradual dosage of
     aspirin, a procedure was scheduled and the patient was brought to the
     endovascular suite.  The guide catheter was then used to selectively
     catheterize the right common carotid artery with an angiographic run revealed
     the presence of diffuse atherosclerotic disease which is unchanged compared to
     previously.  Angiographic run was performed then of the right internal carotid
     and biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography mode which helpded
     define the wide neck of the aneurysm and the pocket of loosely packed coils.
     At this point, a  microcatheter was used coaxially over a 200 cm exchange MPI
     wire.  The MTI X-celerator wire was then used to selectively place the
     microcatheter into the inferior division of the middle cerebral artery on the
     right side. With the microcatheter in this branch, the wire was advanced well
     into M3 branch consistent with the angular branch of the angular division of
     the middle cerebral artery.  The microcatheter was then removed and a
     neuroform stent was guided over the exchange wire and delivered across the
     cerebral artery bifurcation.  This unable us then to keep the stent in
     position.  After deployment an angiographic run was performed which showed no
     evidence of branch occlusion or compromise by the stent deployed.
     Subsequently, the wire was withdrawn up to the middle cerebral artery location
     and the microcatheter  was then used to cross the interstices of the stent
     into the neck residual.  With the microcatheter in the aneurysm, residual
     series of GDC coils were advanced until they were clearly in contact with the
     stent interstices.  At this point, an angiographic run was performed in
     biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography which showed an excellent
     result.  The microcatheter was then withdrawn and a final angiographic run was
     performed in the biplane projection as well as one of the neck which showed no
     evidence of intimal injury to the carotid artery.  At this point, the guide
     catheter was withdrawn.  The patient was then awokened from anesthesia and
     transferred to the post anesthesia care unit in stable condition.
     
     RESULTS:  Persistent 4 mm pocket of the previously treated right middle
     cerebral aneurysm embolized using a combination of GDC coils and neuroform
     stent with an excellent angiographic result with no evidence of iatrogenic
     branch occlusion.
     
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268

     which has left her with mild left-sided hemiparesis.  At the time of her
     initial treatment, the right middle cerebral artery aneurysm which was noted
     to be wide neck could not be treated completely at the neck although the
     rupture site was secured with coils and the patient did an excellent recovery.
     The neck of the aneurysm was relatively loosely packed because its wide neck.
     Accordingly she is undergoing this procedure in order to perform a stent
     mediated coil embolization and packing of the neck of the right middle
     cerebral aneurysm.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient and her son and her husband were given a full and
     complete explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks,
     benefits and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In
     addition the possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection,
     stroke, neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other
     unforeseen complications including the risk of coma and even death were
     outlined.  The patient and her son and her husband understood and wished to
     proceed with the operation.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge signal wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire
     and kept on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right middle
     cerebral artery, right M3 branch of the middle cerebral artery.  After the
     patient has been placed on Plavix and desensitize using gradual dosage of
     aspirin, a procedure was scheduled and the patient was brought to the
     endovascular suite.  The guide catheter was then used to selectively
     catheterize the right common carotid artery with an angiographic run revealed
     the presence of diffuse atherosclerotic disease which is unchanged compared to
     previously.  Angiographic run was performed then of the right internal carotid
     and biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography mode which helpded
     define the wide neck of the aneurysm and the pocket of loosely packed coils.
     At this point, a  microcatheter was used coaxially over a 200 cm exchange MPI
     wire.  The MTI X-celerator wire was then used to selectively place the
     microcatheter into the inferior division of the middle cerebral artery on the
     right side. With the microcatheter in this branch, the wire was advanced well
     into M3 branch consistent with the angular branch of the angular division of
     the middle cerebral artery.  The microcatheter was then removed and a
     neuroform stent was guided over the exchange wire and delivered across the
     cerebral artery bifurcation.  This unable us then to keep the stent in
     position.  After deployment an angiographic run was performed which showed no
     evidence of branch occlusion or compromise by the stent deployed.
     Subsequently, the wire was withdrawn up to the middle cerebral artery location
     and the microcatheter  was then used to cross the interstices of the stent
     into the neck residual.  With the microcatheter in the aneurysm, residual
     series of GDC coils were advanced until they were clearly in contact with the
     stent interstices.  At this point, an angiographic run was performed in
     biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography which showed an excellent
     result.  The microcatheter was then withdrawn and a final angiographic run was
     performed in the biplane projection as well as one of the neck which showed no
     evidence of intimal injury to the carotid artery.  At this point, the guide
     catheter was withdrawn.  The patient was then awokened from anesthesia and
     transferred to the post anesthesia care unit in stable condition.
     
     RESULTS:  Persistent 4 mm pocket of the previously treated right middle
     cerebral aneurysm embolized using a combination of GDC coils and neuroform
     stent with an excellent angiographic result with no evidence of iatrogenic
     branch occlusion.
     
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA

     Accordingly she is undergoing this procedure in order to perform a stent
     mediated coil embolization and packing of the neck of the right middle
     cerebral aneurysm.
     
     CONSENT:  The patient and her son and her husband were given a full and
     complete explanation of the procedure.  Specifically the indications, risks,
     benefits and alternatives to the procedure were explained in detail.  In
     addition the possible complications such as the risk of bleeding, infection,
     stroke, neurological deficit or deterioration, groin hematoma, and other
     unforeseen complications including the risk of coma and even death were
     outlined.  The patient and her son and her husband understood and wished to
     proceed with the operation.
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM
     CAROT/CEREB [**Hospital1 5**]                                                  Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 2180**]
     Reason: IN-PATIENT.  CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAM USING NEUROFORM STENT.
     Admitting Diagnosis: ANEURYSM/SDA
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 268
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:  The patient was brought in the endovascular suite and
     placed on the table in supine position.  The right groin area was prepped and
     draped in the usual sterile fashion.  A 19 gauge signal wall needle was then
     used to puncture the right femoral artery and upon the return of brisk
     arterial blood, a 5 FR vascular sheath was inserted over a guidewire
     and kept on a heparinized saline drip.  Next a diagnostic catheter was used to
     selectively catheterize the following vessels over a guidewire in succession:
     Right common carotid artery, right internal carotid artery, right middle
     cerebral artery, right M3 branch of the middle cerebral artery.  After the
     patient has been placed on Plavix and desensitize using gradual dosage of
     aspirin, a procedure was scheduled and the patient was brought to the
     endovascular suite.  The guide catheter was then used to selectively
     catheterize the right common carotid artery with an angiographic run revealed
     the presence of diffuse atherosclerotic disease which is unchanged compared to
     previously.  Angiographic run was performed then of the right internal carotid
     and biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography mode which helpded
     define the wide neck of the aneurysm and the pocket of loosely packed coils.
     At this point, a  microcatheter was used coaxially over a 200 cm exchange MPI
     wire.  The MTI X-celerator wire was then used to selectively place the
     microcatheter into the inferior division of the middle cerebral artery on the
     right side. With the microcatheter in this branch, the wire was advanced well
     into M3 branch consistent with the angular branch of the angular division of
     the middle cerebral artery.  The microcatheter was then removed and a
     neuroform stent was guided over the exchange wire and delivered across the
     cerebral artery bifurcation.  This unable us then to keep the stent in
     position.  After deployment an angiographic run was performed which showed no
     evidence of branch occlusion or compromise by the stent deployed.
     Subsequently, the wire was withdrawn up to the middle cerebral artery location
     and the microcatheter  was then used to cross the interstices of the stent
     into the neck residual.  With the microcatheter in the aneurysm, residual
     series of GDC coils were advanced until they were clearly in contact with the
     stent interstices.  At this point, an angiographic run was performed in
     biplane and two dimensional rotational angiography which showed an excellent
     result.  The microcatheter was then withdrawn and a final angiographic run was
     performed in the biplane projection as well as one of the neck which showed no
     evidence of intimal injury to the carotid artery.  At this point, the guide
     catheter was withdrawn.  The patient was then awokened from anesthesia and
     transferred to the post anesthesia care unit in stable condition.
     
     RESULTS:  Persistent 4 mm pocket of the previously treated right middle
     cerebral aneurysm embolized using a combination of GDC coils and neuroform
     stent with an excellent angiographic result with no evidence of iatrogenic
     branch occlusion.
     
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**2833-3-8**] 7:41 AM

     Reason: Pt is a 63yo woman with history of an aneurysm, s/p coiling

     UNDERLYING MEDICAL CONDITION:
      63 year old woman with aneurysm, seizures
     REASON FOR THIS EXAMINATION:
      Pt is a 63yo woman with history of an aneurysm, s/p coiling 1 yr ago and
      re-coiling 2 weeks ago after regrowth of aneurysm who presented with new onset
      seizures yesterday.  Pt of Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 50**]
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     INDICATIONS:  Aneurysm recently coiled. New onset of seizure. 
     
     MRI OF THE BRAIN/MRA OF THE CIRCLE OF [**Location (un) 4**]:
     
     TECHNIQUE:   Multiplanar T1 and T2W imaging of the brain was performed.  3D
     time of flight MRA of the Circle of [**Location (un) **] was performed. Multiplanar
     reformatted images and source image data were reviewed.
     
     FINDINGS:  Comparison is made to previous CT scan, the most recent from
     [**2832-9-27**] and the angiogram of [**2833-3-8**].
     
     There is a large area of encephalomalacia involving the right middle cerebral
     arterial territory. There is residual hemosiderin and susceptibility artifact
     within the brain tissue in this location.  No extension of the infarction is
     evident. There is no diffusion signal abnormality to indicate recent
     infarction. There is enlargement of the right lateral ventricle. There is
     volume loss. The left lateral ventricles are not dilated. A left frontal
     ventricular catheter is present and extends across the midline, into the body
     of the right lateral ventricle. There is an old hemorrhagic tract from a left
     ventricular catheter in the left frontal lobes.  A few small foci of increased
     T2 signal are identified in the white matter bilaterally and may represent
     sites of microvascular infarction.
     
     The brain stem and cerebellum appear normal.
     
     Two coiled aneurysms are identified as areas with absent signal, one is just
     to the right of the right anterior communicating artery, and another is at the
     right middle cerebral arterial bifurcation. No flow signal is identified in
     these foci. There is diminished flow evident in the right A1 arterial segment
     and in the right middle cerebral arterial branches.  This is probably related
     to a combination of artifact from coils present and diminished flow related to
     old infarction.  The left internal carotid artery, anterior and middle
     cerebral arteries have normal flow signal.
     
     There is flow identified in the left vertebral artery which continues as the
     basilar artery. There is no flow signal in the expected location of the right
     vertebral artery.    Both posterior cerebral arteries are identified.

     1.  MRI of the brain reveals old hemorrhage and encephalomalacia involving the
